<p>The <b>Central African Republic</b> (<b>CAR</b>; <a href="/wiki/Sango" title="Sango" class="mw-redirect">Sango</a>: <i>Ködörösêse tî Bêafrîka</i><span style="margin-left:1px">;</span> <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <span lang="fr"><i>République centrafricaine</i></span>&#160; <small>pronounced:&#160;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[ʁepyblik sɑ̃tʁafʁikɛn]</a></span>, or <i><span lang="fr">Centrafrique</span></i> <span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA_for_French" title="Help:IPA for French">[sɑ̃tʀafʁik]</a></span>) is a <a href="/wiki/Landlocked_country" title="Landlocked country">landlocked country</a> in <a href="/wiki/Central_Africa" title="Central Africa">Central Africa</a>. It is bordered by <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> to the north, <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a> to the northeast, <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a> to the east, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a> to the south and <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> to the west. The CAR covers a land area of about 620,000 square kilometres (240,000&#160;sq&#160;mi) and had an estimated population of around 4.7 million as of 2014.</p>
<p>Most of the CAR consists of Sudano-Guinean <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savannas</a>, but the country also includes a <a href="/wiki/Sahel" title="Sahel">Sahelo</a>-<a href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna" class="mw-redirect">Sudanian</a> zone in the north and an <a href="/wiki/Northern_Congolian_forest-savanna_mosaic" title="Northern Congolian forest-savanna mosaic">equatorial forest zone</a> in the south. Two thirds of the country is within the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a> basin (which flows into the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo</a>), while the remaining third lies in the basin of the <a href="/wiki/Chari_River" title="Chari River">Chari</a>, which flows into <a href="/wiki/Lake_Chad" title="Lake Chad">Lake Chad</a>.</p>
<p>What is today the Central African Republic has been inhabited for millennia; however, the country's current borders were established by France, which ruled the country as a colony starting in the late 19th century. After gaining independence from France in 1960, the Central African Republic was ruled by a series of autocratic leaders; by the 1990s, calls for democracy led to the first multi-party democratic elections in 1993. <a href="/wiki/Ange-F%C3%A9lix_Patass%C3%A9" title="Ange-Félix Patassé">Ange-Félix Patassé</a> became president, but was later removed by <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Boziz%C3%A9" title="François Bozizé">General François Bozizé</a> in the <a href="/wiki/2003_Central_African_Republic_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="2003 Central African Republic coup d'état">2003 coup</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Bush_War" title="Central African Republic Bush War">Central African Republic Bush War</a> began in 2004 and, despite a peace treaty in 2007 and another in 2011, <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_conflict_(2012%E2%80%93present)" title="Central African Republic conflict (2012–present)">fighting broke out</a> between government, Muslim, and Christian factions in December 2012, leading to ethnic and <a href="/wiki/Religious_cleansing" title="Religious cleansing">religious cleansing</a> and massive population displacement in 2013 and 2014.</p>
<p>Despite its significant <a href="/wiki/Mineral" title="Mineral">mineral</a> deposits and other resources, such as <a href="/wiki/Uranium" title="Uranium">uranium</a> reserves, <a href="/wiki/Crude_oil" title="Crude oil" class="mw-redirect">crude oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gold" title="Gold">gold</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lumber" title="Lumber">lumber</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Hydropower" title="Hydropower">hydropower</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> as well as significant quantities of <a href="/wiki/Arable_land" title="Arable land">arable land</a>, the Central African Republic is among the ten poorest countries in the world. As of 2013, according to the <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> (HDI), the country had a low level of human development, ranking at 185th out of 187 countries.<sup id="cite_ref-HDI_5-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-HDI-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="History of the Central African Republic">History of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_history">Early history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Approximately 10,000 years ago, <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a> forced hunter-gatherer societies south into the Sahel regions of northern Central Africa, where some groups settled and began farming as part of the <a href="/wiki/Neolithic_Revolution" title="Neolithic Revolution">Neolithic Revolution</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Eastern_Africa_2011.2C_pg._4_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eastern_Africa_2011.2C_pg._4-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> Initial farming of <a href="/wiki/Dioscorea_rotundata" title="Dioscorea rotundata">white yam</a> progressed into <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, and before 3000 BC<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> the domestication of <a href="/wiki/Elaeis_guineensis" title="Elaeis guineensis">African oil palm</a> improved the groups' nutrition and allowed for expansion of the local populations.<sup id="cite_ref-10" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Bananas arrived in the region and added an important source of carbohydrates to the diet; they were also used in the production of <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverages" title="Alcoholic beverages" class="mw-redirect">alcoholic beverages</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> This Agricultural Revolution, combined with a "Fish-stew Revolution", in which fishing began to take place, and the use of boats, allowed for the transportation of goods. Products were often moved in <a href="/wiki/Ceramic" title="Ceramic">ceramic</a> pots, which are the first known examples of <a href="/wiki/Artistic_expression" title="Artistic expression" class="mw-redirect">artistic expression</a> from the region's inhabitants.<sup id="cite_ref-Eastern_Africa_2011.2C_pg._4_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Eastern_Africa_2011.2C_pg._4-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Bouar" title="Bouar">Bouar Megaliths</a> in the western region of the country indicate an advanced level of habitation dating back to the very late <a href="/wiki/Neolithic" title="Neolithic">Neolithic Era</a> (c. 3500–2700 BC).<sup id="cite_ref-11" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Ferrous_metallurgy" title="Ferrous metallurgy">Ironworking</a> arrived in the region around 1000 BC from both Bantu cultures in what is today <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a> and from the Nile city of <a href="/wiki/Mero%C3%AB" title="Meroë">Meroë</a>, the capital of the <a href="/wiki/Kingdom_of_Kush" title="Kingdom of Kush">Kingdom of Kush</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/Bantu_expansion" title="Bantu expansion">Bantu Migrations</a> from about 1000 BC to AD 1000, <a href="/wiki/Ubangian" title="Ubangian" class="mw-redirect">Ubangian</a>-speaking people spread eastward from Cameroon to Sudan, <a href="/wiki/Bantu_languages" title="Bantu languages">Bantu</a>-speaking people settled in the southwestern regions of the CAR, and <a href="/wiki/Central_Sudanic" title="Central Sudanic" class="mw-redirect">Central Sudanic</a>-speaking people settled along the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a> in what is today Central and East CAR.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Production of <a href="/wiki/Copper" title="Copper">copper</a>, <a href="/wiki/Salt" title="Salt">salt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dried_fish" title="Dried fish">dried fish</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Textiles" title="Textiles" class="mw-redirect">textiles</a> dominated the economic trade in the Central African region.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="16th.E2.80.9318th_century">16th–18th century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 16th–18th century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>During the 16th and 17th centuries <a href="/wiki/Arab_slave_trade" title="Arab slave trade">Muslim slave traders</a> began to raid the region and their captives were shipped to the Mediterranean coast, Europe, Arabia, the Western Hemisphere, or to the slave ports and factories along the West African coast.<sup id="cite_ref-africanhistory.about.com_15-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanhistory.about.com-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bangi_language" title="Bangi language">Bobangi people</a> became major slave traders<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (June 2014)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> and sold their captives to the Americas using the Ubangi river to reach the coast.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 18th century Bandia-Nzakara peoples established the <a href="/wiki/Bangassou" title="Bangassou">Bangassou</a> Kingdom along the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-africanhistory.about.com_15-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-africanhistory.about.com-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="French_colonial_period">French colonial period</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: French colonial period">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1875 the <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudanese</a> sultan <a href="/wiki/Rabih_az-Zubayr" title="Rabih az-Zubayr">Rabih az-Zubayr</a> governed Upper-Oubangui, which included present-day CAR. The European penetration of Central African territory began in the late 19th century during the <a href="/wiki/Scramble_for_Africa" title="Scramble for Africa">Scramble for Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Europeans, primarily the French, <a href="/wiki/Germans" title="Germans">Germans</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Belgians" title="Belgians">Belgians</a>, arrived in the area in 1885. France created <a href="/wiki/Ubangi-Shari" title="Ubangi-Shari">Ubangi-Shari</a> territory in 1894.</p>
<p>In 1911 at the <a href="/wiki/Treaty_of_Fez" title="Treaty of Fez" class="mw-redirect">Treaty of Fez</a>, France ceded a nearly 300,000&#160;km² portion of the Sangha and Lobaye basins to the <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">German Empire</a> which ceded a smaller area (in present day <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>) to France. After <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> France again annexed the territory.</p>
<p>In 1920 <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a> was established and Ubangi-Shari was administered from <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Francophone_Africa_1997.2C_pg._111_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Francophone_Africa_1997.2C_pg._111-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> During the 1920s and 1930s the French introduced a policy of mandatory cotton cultivation,<sup id="cite_ref-Francophone_Africa_1997.2C_pg._111_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Francophone_Africa_1997.2C_pg._111-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> a network of roads was built, attempts were made to combat <a href="/wiki/African_trypanosomiasis" title="African trypanosomiasis">sleeping sickness</a> and <a href="/wiki/Protestant" title="Protestant" class="mw-redirect">Protestant</a> <a href="/wiki/Mission_(Christianity)" title="Mission (Christianity)">missions</a> were established to spread Christianity. New forms of forced labor were also introduced and a large number of Ubangians were sent to work on the <a href="/wiki/Congo-Ocean_Railway" title="Congo-Ocean Railway" class="mw-redirect">Congo-Ocean Railway</a>. Many of these forced laborers died of exhaustion, illness, or the poor conditions which claimed between 20% and 25% of the 127,000 workers.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg/250px-De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg" width="250" height="169" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg/375px-De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/78/De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg/500px-De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1037" data-file-height="700" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:De_Gaulle_Bangui_1940.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">Charles de Gaulle</a> in Bangui, 1940.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 1928, a major insurrection, the <a href="/wiki/Kongo-Wara_rebellion" title="Kongo-Wara rebellion">Kongo-Wara rebellion</a> or 'war of the hoe handle', broke out in Western Ubangi-Shari and continued for several years. The extent of this insurrection, which was perhaps the largest anti-colonial rebellion in Africa during the interwar years, was carefully hidden from the French public because it provided evidence of strong opposition to French colonial rule and forced labor.</p>
<p>In September 1940, during the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" title="Second World War" class="mw-redirect">Second World War</a>, <a href="/wiki/Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Charles de Gaulle">pro-Gaullist</a> French officers took control of Ubangi-Shari and <a href="/wiki/General_Leclerc" title="General Leclerc" class="mw-redirect">General Leclerc</a> established his headquarters for the <a href="/wiki/Free_French_Forces" title="Free French Forces" class="mw-redirect">Free French Forces</a> in <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1946 <a href="/wiki/Barth%C3%A9l%C3%A9my_Boganda" title="Barthélémy Boganda" class="mw-redirect">Barthélémy Boganda</a> was elected with 9,000 votes to the <a href="/wiki/French_National_Assembly" title="French National Assembly" class="mw-redirect">French National Assembly</a>, becoming the first representative for CAR in the French government. Boganda maintained a political stance against racism and the colonial regime but gradually became disheartened with the French political system and returned to CAR to establish the <a href="/wiki/Movement_for_the_Social_Evolution_of_Black_Africa" title="Movement for the Social Evolution of Black Africa">Movement for the Social Evolution of Black Africa</a> (MESAN) in 1950.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Since_Independence_.281960.29-">Since Independence (1960)-</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Since Independence (1960)-">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi-Shari_parliamentary_election,_1957" title="Ubangi-Shari parliamentary election, 1957" class="mw-redirect">Ubangi-Shari Territorial Assembly election</a> in 1957, MESAN captured 347,000 out of the total 356,000 votes,<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup> and won every legislative seat,<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> which led to Boganda being elected president of the Grand Council of <a href="/wiki/French_Equatorial_Africa" title="French Equatorial Africa">French Equatorial Africa</a> and vice-president of the Ubangi-Shari Government Council.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> Within a year, he declared the establishment of the Central African Republic and served as the country's first prime minister. MESAN continued to exist, but its role was limited.<sup id="cite_ref-Kalck2005p136_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kalck2005p136-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> After Boganda's death in a plane crash on 29 March 1959, his cousin, <a href="/wiki/David_Dacko" title="David Dacko">David Dacko</a>, took control of MESAN and became the country's first president after the CAR had formally received <a href="/wiki/Independence" title="Independence">independence</a> from France. Dacko threw out his political rivals, including former Prime Minister and <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Evolution_Movement_of_Central_Africa" title="Democratic Evolution Movement of Central Africa">Mouvement d'évolution démocratique de l'Afrique centrale</a> (MEDAC), leader <a href="/wiki/Abel_Goumba" title="Abel Goumba">Abel Goumba</a>, who he forced into exile in France. With all opposition parties suppressed by November 1962, Dacko declared MESAN as the official party of the state.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Bokassa_and_the_Central_African_Empire_.281965.E2.80.931979.29">Bokassa and the Central African Empire (1965–1979)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Bokassa and the Central African Empire (1965–1979)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="hatnote">Further information: <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Empire" title="Central African Empire">Central African Empire</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bokassa_colored.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bokassa_colored.png/220px-Bokassa_colored.png" width="220" height="322" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bokassa_colored.png/330px-Bokassa_colored.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f4/Bokassa_colored.png/440px-Bokassa_colored.png 2x" data-file-width="540" data-file-height="790" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bokassa_colored.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Jean-B%C3%A9del_Bokassa" title="Jean-Bédel Bokassa">Jean-Bédel Bokassa</a>, self-crowned <a href="/wiki/Emperor_of_Central_Africa" title="Emperor of Central Africa">Emperor of Central Africa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Bokassa_26-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bokassa-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On 31 December 1965, Dacko was overthrown in the <a href="/wiki/Saint-Sylvestre_coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Saint-Sylvestre coup d'état">Saint-Sylvestre coup d'état</a> by Colonel <a href="/wiki/Jean-B%C3%A9del_Bokassa" title="Jean-Bédel Bokassa">Jean-Bédel Bokassa</a>, who suspended the constitution and dissolved the National Assembly. President Bokassa declared himself President for Life in 1972, and named himself Emperor Bokassa I of the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Empire" title="Central African Empire">Central African Empire</a> (as the country was renamed) on 4 December 1976. A year later, Emperor Bokassa crowned himself in a lavish and expensive ceremony that was ridiculed by much of the world.<sup id="cite_ref-Bokassa_26-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Bokassa-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In April 1979, young students protested against Bokassa's decree that all school attendees would need to buy uniforms from a company owned by one of his wives. The government violently suppressed the protests, killing 100 children and teenagers. Bokassa himself may have been personally involved in some of the killings.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1979, France overthrew Bokassa and "restored" Dacko to power (subsequently restoring the name of the country to the Central African Republic). Dacko, in turn, was again overthrown in a coup by General <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Kolingba" title="André Kolingba">André Kolingba</a> on 1 September 1981.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_African_Republic_under_Kolingba">Central African Republic under Kolingba</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Central African Republic under Kolingba">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Kolingba suspended the constitution and ruled with a military junta until 1985. He introduced a new constitution in 1986 which was adopted by a nationwide referendum. Membership in his new party, the <a href="/wiki/Rassemblement_D%C3%A9mocratique_Centrafricain" title="Rassemblement Démocratique Centrafricain" class="mw-redirect">Rassemblement Démocratique Centrafricain</a> (RDC), was voluntary. In 1987 and 1988, semi-free elections to parliament were held but Kolingba's two major political opponents, <a href="/wiki/Abel_Goumba" title="Abel Goumba">Abel Goumba</a> and <a href="/wiki/Ange-F%C3%A9lix_Patass%C3%A9" title="Ange-Félix Patassé">Ange-Félix Patassé</a> were not allowed to participate.</p>
<p>By 1990, inspired by the fall of the Berlin Wall, a pro-democracy movement arose. Elections were held in 1993 with the help of the international community, Ange-Félix Patassé won in the second round of voting with 53% of the vote while Goumba won 45.6%. Patassé's party, the <i>Mouvement pour la Libération du Peuple Centrafricain</i> (MLPC) or Movement for the Liberation of the Central African People, gained a simple but not an absolute majority of seats in parliament, which meant Patassé's party required coalition partners.</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Patass.C3.A9_Government_.281993.E2.80.932003.29">Patassé Government (1993–2003)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Patassé Government (1993–2003)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<table class="metadata plainlinks ambox ambox-content ambox-one_source" role="presentation">
<tr>
<td class="mbox-image">
<div style="width:52px"><a href="/wiki/File:Question_book-new.svg" class="image"><img alt="Question book-new.svg" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" width="50" height="39" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="262" data-file-height="204" /></a></div>
</td>
<td class="mbox-text"><span class="mbox-text-span">This section <b>relies largely or entirely upon a <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Identifying_reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Identifying reliable sources">single source</a></b>. <span class="hide-when-compact">Relevant discussion may be found on the <a href="/wiki/Talk:Central_African_Republic#.23" title="Talk:Central African Republic">talk page</a>. Please help <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit">improve this article</a> by introducing <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citing_sources" title="Wikipedia:Citing sources">citations</a> to additional sources.</span> <small><i>(January 2015)</i></small></span></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p>Patassé purged many of the Kolingba elements from the government and Kolingba supporters accused Patassé's government of conducting a "witch hunt" against the Yakoma. A new constitution was approved on 28 December 1994 but had little impact on the country's politics. In 1996–1997, reflecting steadily decreasing public confidence in the government's erratic behaviour, three mutinies against Patassé's administration were accompanied by widespread destruction of property and heightened ethnic tension. During this time (1996) the Peace Corps evacuated all its volunteers to neighboring Cameroon. To date, the Peace Corps has not returned to the Central African Republic. The <a href="/wiki/Bangui_Agreements" title="Bangui Agreements">Bangui Agreements</a>, signed in January 1997, provided for the deployment of an inter-African military mission, to Central African Republic and re-entry of ex-mutineers into the government on 7 April 1997. The inter-African military mission was later replaced by a U.N. <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council_Resolution_1159" title="United Nations Security Council Resolution 1159">peacekeeping force (MINURCA)</a>.</p>
<p>In 1998, parliamentary elections resulted in Kolingba's RDC winning 20 out of 109 seats but in 1999, in spite of widespread public anger in urban centers over his corrupt rule, Patassé won a second term in the presidential election.</p>
<p>On 28 May 2001, rebels stormed strategic buildings in Bangui in an unsuccessful coup attempt. The army chief of staff, Abel Abrou, and General François N'Djadder Bedaya were killed, but Patassé regained the upper hand by bringing in at least 300 troops of the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Congolese</a> rebel leader <a href="/wiki/Jean-Pierre_Bemba" title="Jean-Pierre Bemba">Jean-Pierre Bemba</a> and Libyan soldiers.<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In the aftermath of the failed <a href="/wiki/Coup_d%27%C3%A9tat" title="Coup d'état">coup</a>, militias loyal to Patassé sought revenge against rebels in many neighborhoods of <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a> and incited unrest including the murder of many political opponents. Eventually, Patassé came to suspect that General <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Boziz%C3%A9" title="François Bozizé">François Bozizé</a> was involved in another coup attempt against him, which led Bozizé to flee with loyal troops to Chad. In March 2003, Bozizé launched a surprise attack against Patassé, who was out of the country. Libyan troops and some 1,000 soldiers of Bemba's Congolese rebel organization failed to stop the rebels and Bozizé's forces succeeded in overthrowing Patassé.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Central_African_Republic_since_2003">Central African Republic since 2003</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Central African Republic since 2003">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg/250px-Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg" width="250" height="167" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg/375px-Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/bb/Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg/500px-Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3072" data-file-height="2048" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rebel_in_northern_CAR_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Rebel militia in the northern countryside, 2007.</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Bush_War" title="Central African Republic Bush War">Central African Republic Bush War</a> and <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Conflict" title="Central African Republic Conflict" class="mw-redirect">Central African Republic Conflict</a></div>
<p>François Bozizé suspended the constitution and named a new cabinet which included most opposition parties. Abel Goumba was named vice-president, which gave Bozizé's new government a positive image. Bozizé established a broad-based National Transition Council to draft a new constitution and announced that he would step down and run for office once the new constitution was approved.</p>
<p>In 2004 the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Bush_War" title="Central African Republic Bush War">Central African Republic Bush War</a> began as forces opposed to Bozizé took up arms against his government. In May 2005 Bozizé won a presidential election that excluded Patassé and in 2006 fighting continued between the government and the rebels. In November 2006, Bozizé's government requested French military support to help them repel rebels who had taken control of towns in the country's northern regions.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20061114_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20061114-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup> Though the initially public details of the agreement pertained to logistics and intelligence, the French assistance eventually included strikes by Mirage jets against rebel positions.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20061130_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20061130-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Syrte Agreement in February and the Birao Peace Agreement in April 2007 called for a cessation of hostilities, the billeting of <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Front_of_the_Central_African_People" title="Democratic Front of the Central African People">FDPC</a> fighters and their integration with FACA, the liberation of political prisoners, integration of FDPC into government, an amnesty for the <a href="/wiki/Union_of_Democratic_Forces_for_Unity" title="Union of Democratic Forces for Unity">UFDR</a>, its recognition as a political party, and the integration of its fighters into the national army. Several groups continued to fight but other groups signed on to the agreement, or similar agreements with the government (e.g. UFR on 15 December 2008). The only major group not to sign an agreement at the time was the <a href="/wiki/Convention_of_Patriots_for_Justice_and_Peace" title="Convention of Patriots for Justice and Peace">CPJP</a>, which continued its activities and signed a peace agreement with the government on 25 August 2012.</p>
<p>In 2011 Bozizé was reelected in an election which was widely considered fraudulent.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2012, <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A9l%C3%A9ka" title="Séléka">Séléka</a>, a coalition of rebel groups, took over towns in the northern and central regions of the country. These groups eventually reached a peace deal with the Bozizé's government in January 2013 involving a power sharing government<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> but this deal broke down and the rebels seized the capital in March 2013 and Bozizé fled the country.<sup id="cite_ref-cnn20130324_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cnn20130324-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-nyt20130325_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-nyt20130325-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Michel_Djotodia" title="Michel Djotodia">Michel Djotodia</a> took over as president and in May 2013 Central African Republic's Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Tiangaye" title="Nicolas Tiangaye">Nicolas Tiangaye</a> requested a <a href="/wiki/UN" title="UN" class="mw-redirect">UN</a> peacekeeping force from the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council" class="mw-redirect">UN Security Council</a> and on 31 May former President Bozizé was indicted for crimes against humanity and incitement of genocide.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup> The security situation did not improve during June–August 2013 and there were reports of over 200,000 <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_persons" title="Internally displaced persons" class="mw-redirect">internally displaced persons</a> (IDPs) as well as human rights abuses<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> and renewed fighting between <i>Séléka</i> and Bozizé supporters.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Chadian_Eland_Mk7.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Chadian_Eland_Mk7.jpg/250px-Chadian_Eland_Mk7.jpg" width="250" height="141" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Chadian_Eland_Mk7.jpg/375px-Chadian_Eland_Mk7.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b4/Chadian_Eland_Mk7.jpg/500px-Chadian_Eland_Mk7.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1349" data-file-height="759" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Chadian_Eland_Mk7.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Eland_Mk7" title="Eland Mk7">Eland</a> armoured car of the Central African Multinational Force patrols the streets of Bangui in December 2013.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p><a href="/wiki/President_of_France" title="President of France">French President</a> <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Hollande" title="François Hollande">François Hollande</a> called on the <a href="/wiki/UN_Security_Council" title="UN Security Council" class="mw-redirect">UN Security Council</a> and <a href="/wiki/African_Union" title="African Union">African Union</a> to increase their efforts to stabilize the country. The <i>Séléka</i> government was said to be divided.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> and in September 2013, Djotodia officially disbanded Seleka, but many rebels refused to disarm and veered further out of government control.<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianNov13_37-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianNov13-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The conflict worsened towards the end of the year with international warnings of a "genocide"<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> and fighting was largely from reprisal attacks on civilians from Seleka's predominantly Muslim fighters and Christian militias called "<a href="/wiki/Anti-balaka" title="Anti-balaka">anti-balaka</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-GuardianNov13_37-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GuardianNov13-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On 11 January 2014, Michael Djotodia and his prime minister, Nicolas Tiengaye, resigned as part of a deal negotiated at a regional summit in neighboring <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Samba-Panza" title="Catherine Samba-Panza">Catherine Samba-Panza</a> was elected as interim president by the National Transitional Council,<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> assuming office on 23 January.</p>
<p>On 18 February 2014, <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> called on the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Security_Council" title="United Nations Security Council">UN Security Council</a> to immediately deploy 3,000 troops to the country to combat what he described as innocent civilians being deliberately targeted and murdered in large numbers. The secretary-general outlined a six-point plan, including the addition of 3,000 peacekeepers to bolster the 6,000 African Union soldiers and 2,000 French troops already deployed in the country.</p>
<p>On 23 July 2014, following Congolese mediation efforts, Séléka and anti-balaka representatives signed a ceasefire agreement in <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Geography of the Central African Republic">Geography of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg/220px-Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg" width="220" height="331" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg/330px-Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a3/Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg/440px-Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2368" data-file-height="3567" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Republique_Centrafricaine_-_Boali_-_Chutes_de_Boali.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Falls of Boali on the Mbali River</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CARvillagefromthesky.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CARvillagefromthesky.jpg/220px-CARvillagefromthesky.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CARvillagefromthesky.jpg/330px-CARvillagefromthesky.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/be/CARvillagefromthesky.jpg/440px-CARvillagefromthesky.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CARvillagefromthesky.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A village in the Central African Republic</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Central African Republic is a landlocked nation within the interior of the African continent. It is bordered by Cameroon, Chad, Sudan, South Sudan, the Democratic Republic of the Congo, and the Republic of the Congo. The country lies between latitudes <a href="/wiki/2nd_parallel_north" title="2nd parallel north">2°</a> and <a href="/wiki/11th_parallel_north" title="11th parallel north">11°N</a>, and longitudes <a href="/wiki/14th_meridian_east" title="14th meridian east">14°</a> and <a href="/wiki/28th_meridian_east" title="28th meridian east">28°E</a>.</p>
<p>Much of the country consists of flat or rolling plateau <a href="/wiki/Savanna" title="Savanna">savanna</a> approximately 500 metres (1,640&#160;ft) above <a href="/wiki/Sea_level" title="Sea level">sea level</a>. Most of the northern half lies within the <a href="/wiki/World_Wildlife_Fund" title="World Wildlife Fund" class="mw-redirect">World Wildlife Fund</a>'s <a href="/wiki/East_Sudanian_savanna" title="East Sudanian savanna" class="mw-redirect">East Sudanian savanna</a> <a href="/wiki/Ecoregion" title="Ecoregion">ecoregion</a>. In addition to the Fertit Hills in the northeast of the CAR, there are scattered hills in the southwest regions. In the northwest is the Yade Massif, a <a href="/wiki/Granite" title="Granite">granite</a> plateau with an altitude of 348 metres (1,143&#160;ft).</p>
<p>At 622,941 square kilometres (240,519&#160;sq&#160;mi), the Central African Republic is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_and_dependencies_by_area" title="List of countries and dependencies by area">world's 45th-largest country</a>. It is comparable in size to <a href="/wiki/Ukraine" title="Ukraine">Ukraine</a>.</p>
<p>Much of the southern border is formed by <a href="/wiki/Tributary" title="Tributary">tributaries</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Congo_River" title="Congo River">Congo River</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Mbomou_River" title="Mbomou River">Mbomou River</a> in the east merges with the <a href="/wiki/Uele_River" title="Uele River">Uele River</a> to form the <a href="/wiki/Ubangi_River" title="Ubangi River">Ubangi River</a>, which also comprises portions of the southern border. The <a href="/wiki/Sangha_River" title="Sangha River">Sangha River</a> flows through some of the western regions of the country, while the eastern border lies along the edge of the <a href="/wiki/Nile_River" title="Nile River" class="mw-redirect">Nile River</a> <a href="/wiki/Drainage_basin" title="Drainage basin">watershed</a>.</p>
<p>It has been estimated that up to 8% of the country is covered by forest, with the densest parts generally located in the southern regions. The forests are highly diverse and include commercially important species of <a href="/wiki/Ayous" title="Ayous" class="mw-redirect">Ayous</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sapele" title="Sapele">Sapelli</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sipo_(timber)" title="Sipo (timber)" class="mw-redirect">Sipo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The deforestation rate is about 0.4% per annum, and <a href="/wiki/Illegal_logging" title="Illegal logging">lumber poaching</a> is commonplace.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2008, Central African Republic was the world's least <a href="/wiki/Light_pollution" title="Light pollution">light pollution</a> affected country.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The Central African Republic is the focal point of the <a href="/wiki/Bangui_Magnetic_Anomaly" title="Bangui Magnetic Anomaly" class="mw-redirect">Bangui Magnetic Anomaly</a>, one of the largest magnetic anomalies on Earth.<sup id="cite_ref-LPI_46-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-LPI-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Wildlife">Wildlife</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Wildlife">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the southwest, the Dzanga-Sangha National Park is located in a rain forest area. The country is noted for its population of <a href="/wiki/Forest_elephant" title="Forest elephant" class="mw-redirect">forest elephants</a> and <a href="/wiki/Western_lowland_gorilla" title="Western lowland gorilla">western lowland gorillas</a>. In the north, the <a href="/wiki/Manovo-Gounda_St_Floris_National_Park" title="Manovo-Gounda St Floris National Park" class="mw-redirect">Manovo-Gounda St Floris National Park</a> is well-populated with wildlife, including <a href="/wiki/Leopard" title="Leopard">leopards</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lion" title="Lion">lions</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Rhinoceros" title="Rhinoceros">rhinos</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/Bamingui-Bangoran_National_Park" title="Bamingui-Bangoran National Park" class="mw-redirect">Bamingui-Bangoran National Park</a> is located in the northeast of CAR. The parks have been seriously affected by the activities of poachers, particularly those from <a href="/wiki/Sudan" title="Sudan">Sudan</a>, over the past two decades.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Needed for the whole paragraph (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Climate_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Climate of the Central African Republic" class="mw-redirect">Climate of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>The climate of the Central African Republic is generally <a href="/wiki/Tropics" title="Tropics">tropical</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Wet_season" title="Wet season">wet season</a> that lasts from June to September in the northern regions of the country, and from May to October in the south. During the wet season, rainstorms are an almost daily occurrence, and early morning <a href="/wiki/Fog" title="Fog">fog</a> is commonplace. Maximum annual precipitation is approximately 1,800 millimetres (71&#160;in) in the upper Ubangi region.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The northern areas are hot and humid from February to May,<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> but can be subject to the hot, dry, and dusty <a href="/wiki/Trade_wind" title="Trade wind">trade wind</a> known as the <a href="/wiki/Harmattan" title="Harmattan">Harmattan</a>. The southern regions have a more equatorial climate, but they are subject to <a href="/wiki/Desertification" title="Desertification">desertification</a>, while the extreme northeast regions of the country are already <a href="/wiki/Desert" title="Desert">desert</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Prefectures_and_sub-prefectures">Prefectures and sub-prefectures</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Prefectures and sub-prefectures">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Prefectures of the Central African Republic">Prefectures of the Central African Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sub-prefectures_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Sub-prefectures of the Central African Republic">Sub-prefectures of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:452px;">
