<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CAR_map_of_prefectures.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A clickable map of the fourteen prefectures of the Central African Republic.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The Central African Republic is divided into 16 administrative <a href="/wiki/Prefecture" title="Prefecture">prefectures</a> (<i>préfectures</i>), two of which are economic prefectures (<i>préfectures economiques</i>), and one an autonomous <a href="/wiki/Commune_(subnational_entity)" title="Commune (subnational entity)" class="mw-redirect">commune</a>; the prefectures are further divided into 71 sub-prefectures (<i>sous-préfectures</i>).</p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Prefectures_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Prefectures of the Central African Republic">prefectures</a> are <a href="/wiki/Bamingui-Bangoran" title="Bamingui-Bangoran">Bamingui-Bangoran</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basse-Kotto" title="Basse-Kotto">Basse-Kotto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haute-Kotto" title="Haute-Kotto">Haute-Kotto</a>, <a href="/wiki/Haut-Mbomou" title="Haut-Mbomou">Haut-Mbomou</a>, <a href="/wiki/K%C3%A9mo" title="Kémo">Kémo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lobaye" title="Lobaye">Lobaye</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mamb%C3%A9r%C3%A9-Kad%C3%A9%C3%AF" title="Mambéré-Kadéï">Mambéré-Kadéï</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mbomou" title="Mbomou">Mbomou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nana-Mamb%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Nana-Mambéré">Nana-Mambéré</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ombella-M%27Poko" title="Ombella-M'Poko">Ombella-M'Poko</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouaka" title="Ouaka">Ouaka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouham" title="Ouham">Ouham</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ouham-Pend%C3%A9" title="Ouham-Pendé">Ouham-Pendé</a> and <a href="/wiki/Vakaga" title="Vakaga">Vakaga</a>. The economic prefectures are <a href="/wiki/Nana-Gr%C3%A9bizi" title="Nana-Grébizi">Nana-Grébizi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sangha-Mba%C3%A9r%C3%A9" title="Sangha-Mbaéré">Sangha-Mbaéré</a>, while the commune is the capital city of <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg/220px-Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg/330px-Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg/440px-Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1024" data-file-height="683" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Group_of_Peul_women_in_Paoua.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Fula women in <a href="/wiki/Paoua" title="Paoua">Paoua</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Demographics of the Central African Republic">Demographics of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>The population of the Central African Republic has almost quadrupled since independence. In 1960, the population was 1,232,000; as of a 2014 UN estimate, it is approximately 4,709,000.<sup id="cite_ref-unpop_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unpop-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> estimates that approximately 11% of the population aged between 15 and 49 is <a href="/wiki/HIV" title="HIV">HIV</a> positive.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup> Only 3% of the country has <a href="/wiki/Antiretroviral" title="Antiretroviral" class="mw-redirect">antiretroviral</a> therapy available, compared to a 17% coverage in the neighbouring countries of <a href="/wiki/Chad" title="Chad">Chad</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Republic of the Congo">Republic of the Congo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The nation is divided into over 80 ethnic groups, each having its own language. The largest ethnic groups are the <a href="/wiki/Gbaya_people" title="Gbaya people">Baya</a>, <a href="/wiki/Banda_people" title="Banda people">Banda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mandjia" title="Mandjia" class="mw-redirect">Mandjia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sara_people" title="Sara people">Sara</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Mboum&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Mboum (page does not exist)">Mboum</a>, <a href="/wiki/M%27Baka" title="M'Baka" class="mw-redirect">M'Baka</a>, <a href="/wiki/Yakoma_people" title="Yakoma people">Yakoma</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fula_people" title="Fula people">Fula or Fulani</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> with others including Europeans of mostly French descent.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_7-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Religion in the Central African Republic">Religion in the Central African Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Niem_(RCA)_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg/220px-Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg/330px-Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/47/Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg/440px-Niem_%28RCA%29_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3008" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Niem_(RCA)_-_Eglise_de_brousse_1.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
A Christian church in the Central African Republic.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>According to the 2003 national census, 80.3% of the population is <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christian</a>—51.4% <a href="/wiki/Protestantism" title="Protestantism">Protestant</a> and 28.9% <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholicism" title="Roman Catholicism" class="mw-redirect">Roman Catholic</a>—and 15% is <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Muslim</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Indigenous belief (<a href="/wiki/Animism" title="Animism">animism</a>) is also practiced, and many indigenous beliefs are incorporated into Christian and Islamic practice.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup> A UN director described religious tensions between Muslims and Christians as being high.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/CIA_World_Factbook" title="CIA World Factbook" class="mw-redirect">CIA World Factbook</a> reports that approximately fifty percent of the population of CAR are <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christians</a> (Protestant 25%, Roman Catholic 25%), while 35% of the population maintain <a href="/wiki/Indigenous_peoples" title="Indigenous peoples">indigenous</a> beliefs and 15% practice <a href="/wiki/Islam" title="Islam">Islam</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_7-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> though it is unclear how recent this information is.</p>
<p>There are many missionary groups operating in the country, including <a href="/wiki/Lutheranism" title="Lutheranism">Lutherans</a>, <a href="/wiki/Baptists" title="Baptists">Baptists</a>, <a href="/wiki/Catholicism" title="Catholicism">Catholics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fellowship_of_Grace_Brethren_Churches" title="Fellowship of Grace Brethren Churches">Grace Brethren</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Jehovah%27s_Witnesses" title="Jehovah's Witnesses">Jehovah's Witnesses</a>. While these missionaries are predominantly from the United States, France, Italy, and Spain, many are also from <a href="/wiki/Nigeria" title="Nigeria">Nigeria</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Democratic_Republic_of_the_Congo" title="Democratic Republic of the Congo">Democratic Republic of the Congo</a>, and other African countries. Large numbers of missionaries left the country when fighting broke out between rebel and government forces in 2002–3, but many of them have now returned to continue their work.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language">Language</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Language">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Languages_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Languages of the Central African Republic">Languages of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>The Central African Republic's two official languages are <a href="/wiki/Sangho" title="Sangho" class="mw-redirect">Sangho</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Ngbandi_language" title="Ngbandi language">Ngbandi</a>-based <a href="/wiki/Creole_language" title="Creole language">creole</a>, and <a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_African_writers_(by_country)#Central_African_Republic" title="List of African writers (by country)" class="mw-redirect">List of African writers (by country) § Central African Republic</a> and <a href="/wiki/Music_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Music of the Central African Republic">Music of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Sports">Sports</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Sports">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_national_football_team" title="Central African Republic national football team">Central African Republic national football team</a>, which is governed by the <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9d%C3%A9ration_Centrafricaine_de_Football" title="Fédération Centrafricaine de Football">Fédération Centrafricaine de Football</a>, stages matches at <a href="/wiki/Barthelemy_Boganda_Stadium" title="Barthelemy Boganda Stadium">Barthelemy Boganda Stadium</a>.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Politics of the Central African Republic">Politics of the Central African Republic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Council_of_Ministers" title="Central African Republic Council of Ministers">Central African Republic Council of Ministers</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_political_parties_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="List of political parties in the Central African Republic">List of political parties in the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>Politics in the Central African Republic formally take place in a framework of a <a href="/wiki/Semi-presidential_system" title="Semi-presidential system">semi-presidential</a> <a href="/wiki/Republic" title="Republic">republic</a>. In this system, the <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_state_of_the_Central_African_Republic_(and_Central_African_Empire)" title="Heads of state of the Central African Republic (and Central African Empire)" class="mw-redirect">President</a> is the <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">head of state</a>, with a <a href="/wiki/Heads_of_government_of_the_Central_African_Republic_(and_Central_African_Empire)" title="Heads of government of the Central African Republic (and Central African Empire)" class="mw-redirect">Prime Minister</a> as <a href="/wiki/Head_of_government" title="Head of government">head of government</a>. <a href="/wiki/Executive_power" title="Executive power" class="mw-redirect">Executive power</a> is exercised by the government. <a href="/wiki/Legislative_power" title="Legislative power" class="mw-redirect">Legislative power</a> is vested in both the government and parliament.</p>
<p>Changes in government have occurred in recent years by three methods: violence, negotiations, and elections. A new constitution was approved by voters in a referendum held on 5 December 2004. The government was rated 'Partly Free' from 1991 to 2001 and from 2004 to 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Executive_branch">Executive branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Executive branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The president is elected by popular vote for a six-year term, and the prime minister is appointed by the president. The president also appoints and presides over the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_Council_of_Ministers" title="Central African Republic Council of Ministers">Council of Ministers</a>, which initiates laws and oversees government operations. As of June 2014 the Central African Republic was governed by an interim government under <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Samba-Panza" title="Catherine Samba-Panza">Catherine Samba-Panza</a>, Interim President; and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Nzapayek%C3%A9" title="André Nzapayeké">André Nzapayeké</a>, Interim Prime Minister.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Legislative_branch">Legislative branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Legislative branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/National_Assembly_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="National Assembly of the Central African Republic" class="mw-redirect">National Assembly</a> (<i>Assemblée Nationale</i>) has 105 members, elected for a five-year term using the two-round (or <a href="/wiki/Two-round_system" title="Two-round system">Run-off</a>) system.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_branch">Judicial branch</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Judicial branch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Like many other former French colonies, the Central African Republic's legal system is based on <a href="/wiki/French_law" title="French law" class="mw-redirect">French law</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> The Supreme Court, or <i>Cour Supreme</i>, is made up of judges appointed by the president. There is also a Constitutional Court, and its judges are also appointed by the president.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_relations">Foreign relations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Foreign relations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Armed_Forces" title="Central African Armed Forces">Central African Armed Forces</a> and <a href="/wiki/Foreign_relations_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Foreign relations of the Central African Republic">Foreign relations of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Foreign_aid_and_UN_Involvement">Foreign aid and UN Involvement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Foreign aid and UN Involvement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>The Central African Republic is heavily dependent upon foreign <a href="/wiki/Aid" title="Aid">aid</a> and numerous <a href="/wiki/NGO" title="NGO" class="mw-redirect">NGOs</a> provide services that the government does not provide.</p>
<p>In 2006, due to ongoing violence, over 50,000 people in the country's northwest were at risk of starvation<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> but this was averted due to assistance from the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (December 2007)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> On 8 January 2008, the UN Secretary-General Ban Ki-Moon declared that the Central African Republic was eligible to receive assistance from the Peacebuilding Fund.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> Three priority areas were identified: first, the reform of the security sector; second, the promotion of good governance and the rule of law; and third, the revitalization of communities affected by conflicts. On 12 June 2008, the Central African Republic requested assistance from the <a href="/wiki/UN_Peacebuilding_Commission" title="UN Peacebuilding Commission" class="mw-redirect">UN Peacebuilding Commission</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> which was set up in 2005 to help countries emerging from conflict avoid devolving back into war or chaos.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Events_in_2013.E2.80.932014">Events in 2013–2014</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Events in 2013–2014">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Central_African_Republic_conflict_(2012%E2%80%932014)" title="Central African Republic conflict (2012–2014)" class="mw-redirect">Central African Republic conflict (2012–2014)</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:242px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19,_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19%2C_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg/240px-thumbnail.jpg" width="240" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19%2C_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg/360px-thumbnail.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19%2C_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg/480px-thumbnail.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6016" data-file-height="3693" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Refugees_of_the_fighting_in_the_Central_African_Republic_observe_Rwandan_soldiers_being_dropped_off_at_Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport_in_the_Central_African_Republic_Jan._19,_2014_140119-F-RN211-760.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Refugee" title="Refugee">Refugees</a> of the fighting in the Central African Republic, January 2014</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In March 2013 the Bozizé government fell to the <a href="/wiki/2012%E2%80%9313_Central_African_Republic_conflict" title="2012–13 Central African Republic conflict" class="mw-redirect">Séléka rebel group</a> and the rebel leader, Djotodia, proclaimed himself President, while <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Tiangaye" title="Nicolas Tiangaye">Nicolas Tiangaye</a> remained as the <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a>; he had recently been appointed and was allowed by the Séléka rebels to retain his post, as he was endorsed by the opposition.<sup id="cite_ref-mg20130326_61-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mg20130326-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A new government was appointed on 31 March 2013, which consisted of members of Séléka and representatives of the opposition to Bozizé, one pro-Bozizé individual,<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> and a number representatives of civil society. On 1 April, the former opposition parties declared that they would boycott the government.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> After African leaders in Chad refused to recognize Djotodia as President, proposing to form a transitional council and the holding of new elections, Djotodia signed a decree on 6 April for the formation of a council that would act as a transitional parliament. The council was tasked with electing a president to serve prior to elections in 18 months.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2013, the United Nations Secretary-General <a href="/wiki/Ban_Ki-moon" title="Ban Ki-moon">Ban Ki-moon</a> noted that the security situation in the country remained precarious with government authority nonexistent outside of Bangui.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Both the president and prime minister resigned through an announcement at a regional summit in January 2014, after which an interim leader and speaker for the provisional parliament took over.<sup id="cite_ref-bbc20140110_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20140110-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-bbc20140113_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bbc20140113-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup> In late January <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Samba-Panza" title="Catherine Samba-Panza">Catherine Samba-Panza</a> became the Interim President, and <a href="/wiki/Andr%C3%A9_Nzapayek%C3%A9" title="André Nzapayeké">André Nzapayeké</a>, the Interim Prime Minister.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg/220px-Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg/330px-Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/48/Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg/440px-Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="533" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Bangui_Shopping_District.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a> shopping district</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Economy of the Central African Republic">Economy of the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>The currency of Central African Republic is the <a href="/wiki/Central_African_CFA_franc" title="Central African CFA franc">CFA franc</a>, which is accepted across the former countries of French West Africa and trades at a fixed rate to the Euro. Diamonds constitute the country's most important export, accounting for 40–55% of export revenues, but it is estimated that between 30% and 50% of those produced each year leave the country clandestinely.</p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg/220px-Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg/330px-Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg/440px-Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="1104" data-file-height="863" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Tree_map_export_2009_Central_African_Republic.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Graphical depiction of Central African Republic's product exports in 28 color-coded categories</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Agriculture is dominated by the cultivation and sale of food crops such as <a href="/wiki/Cassava" title="Cassava">cassava</a>, <a href="/wiki/Peanut" title="Peanut">peanuts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Maize" title="Maize">maize</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sorghum" title="Sorghum">sorghum</a>, <a href="/wiki/Millet" title="Millet">millet</a>, <a href="/wiki/Sesame" title="Sesame">sesame</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Plantain_(cooking)" title="Plantain (cooking)" class="mw-redirect">plantain</a>. The annual real GDP <a href="/wiki/Economic_growth" title="Economic growth">growth rate</a> is just above 3%. The importance of food crops over exported <a href="/wiki/Cash_crops" title="Cash crops" class="mw-redirect">cash crops</a> is indicated by the fact that the total production of cassava, the staple food of most Central Africans, ranges between 200,000 and 300,000 <a href="/wiki/Tonnes" title="Tonnes" class="mw-redirect">tonnes</a> a year, while the production of <a href="/wiki/Cotton" title="Cotton">cotton</a>, the principal exported cash crop, ranges from 25,000 to 45,000 tonnes a year. Food crops are not exported in large quantities, but still constitute the principal cash crops of the country, because Central Africans derive far more income from the periodic sale of surplus food crops than from exported cash crops such as cotton or coffee.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Needed for the whole paragraph (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Much of the country is self-sufficient in food crops; however, <a href="/wiki/Livestock" title="Livestock">livestock</a> development is hindered by the presence of the <a href="/wiki/Tsetse_fly" title="Tsetse fly">tsetse fly</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (June 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The Republic's primary import partner is the <a href="/wiki/Netherlands" title="Netherlands">Netherlands</a> (19.5%). Other imports come from <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a> (9.7%), France (9.3%), and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (8.7%). Its largest export partner is Belgium (31.5%), followed by China (27.7%), the Democratic Republic of Congo (8.6%), <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">Indonesia</a> (5.2%), and France (4.5%).<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_7-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/Per_capita_income" title="Per capita income">per capita income</a> of the Republic is often listed as being approximately $400 a year, <a href="/wiki/List_of_countries_by_GNI_(PPP)_per_capita" title="List of countries by GNI (PPP) per capita">one of the lowest in the world</a>, but this figure is based mostly on reported sales of exports and largely ignores the unregistered sale of foods, locally produced <a href="/wiki/Alcoholic_beverage" title="Alcoholic beverage">alcoholic beverages</a>, <a href="/wiki/Diamond" title="Diamond">diamonds</a>, <a href="/wiki/Ivory" title="Ivory">ivory</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bushmeat" title="Bushmeat">bushmeat</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Traditional_medicine" title="Traditional medicine">traditional medicine</a>. For most Central Africans, the <a href="/wiki/Informal_economy" title="Informal economy" class="mw-redirect">informal economy</a> of the CAR is more important than the formal economy.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Needed for the whole paragraph (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>Export trade is hindered by poor economic development and the country's landlocked position.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="Needed for the whole paragraph (October 2010)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>The CAR is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Organization_for_the_Harmonization_of_Business_Law_in_Africa" title="Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa" class="mw-redirect">Organization for the Harmonization of Business Law in Africa</a> (OHADA). In the 2009 <a href="/wiki/World_Bank_Group" title="World Bank Group">World Bank Group</a>'s report <i>Doing Business</i>, it was ranked 183rd of 183 as regards 'ease of doing business', a <a href="/wiki/Composite_(finance)" title="Composite (finance)">composite index</a> which takes into account regulations that enhance business activity and those that restrict it.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Infrastructure">Infrastructure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Infrastructure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Transportation">Transportation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Transportation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Transportation_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Transportation in the Central African Republic" class="mw-redirect">Transportation in the Central African Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg/220px-Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg/330px-Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/29/Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg/440px-Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Central_African_Republic_-_Trucks_in_Bangui.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Trucks in Bangui</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Bangui is the transport hub of the Central African Republic. As of 1999, eight roads connected the city to other main towns in the country, <a href="/wiki/Cameroon" title="Cameroon">Cameroon</a>, Chad and <a href="/wiki/South_Sudan" title="South Sudan">South Sudan</a>; of these, only the toll roads are paved. During the rainy season from July to October, some roads are impassable.<sup id="cite_ref-e200_70-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e200-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>River <a href="/wiki/Ferry" title="Ferry">ferries</a> sail from the <a href="/wiki/River_port" title="River port" class="mw-redirect">river port</a> at Bangui to <a href="/wiki/Brazzaville" title="Brazzaville">Brazzaville</a> and <a href="/wiki/Zongo" title="Zongo">Zongo</a>. The river can be navigated most of the year between Bangui and Brazzaville. From Brazzaville, goods are transported by rail to <a href="/wiki/Pointe-Noire" title="Pointe-Noire">Pointe-Noire</a>, Congo's Atlantic port.<sup id="cite_ref-Finanace_72-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Finanace-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup> The river port handles the overwhelming majority of the country's international trade and has a cargo handling capacity of 350,000 tons; it has 350 metres (1,150&#160;ft) length of <a href="/wiki/Wharfs" title="Wharfs" class="mw-redirect">wharfs</a> and 24,000 square metres (260,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of warehousing space.<sup id="cite_ref-e200_70-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-e200-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Bangui_M%27Poko_International_Airport" title="Bangui M'Poko International Airport">Bangui M'Poko International Airport</a> is Central African Republic's only international airport. As of June 2014 it had regularly scheduled direct flights to <a href="/wiki/Maya-Maya_Airport" title="Maya-Maya Airport">Brazzaville</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mohammed_V_International_Airport" title="Mohammed V International Airport">Casablanca</a>, <a href="/wiki/Cadjehoun_Airport" title="Cadjehoun Airport">Cotonou</a>, <a href="/wiki/Douala_International_Airport" title="Douala International Airport">Douala</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%27djili_Airport" title="N'djili Airport">Kinshasha</a>, <a href="/wiki/Lom%C3%A9-Tokoin_Airport" title="Lomé-Tokoin Airport" class="mw-redirect">Lomé</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quatro_de_Fevereiro_Airport" title="Quatro de Fevereiro Airport">Luanda</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malabo_International_Airport" title="Malabo International Airport">Malabo</a>, <a href="/wiki/N%27Djamena_International_Airport" title="N'Djamena International Airport">N'Djamena</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paris-Charles_de_Gaulle" title="Paris-Charles de Gaulle" class="mw-redirect">Paris</a>, <a href="/wiki/Pointe_Noire_Airport" title="Pointe Noire Airport">Pointe-Noire</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Yaound%C3%A9_Nsimalen_International_Airport" title="Yaoundé Nsimalen International Airport">Yaoundé</a>.</p>
<p>Since at least 2002 there have been plans to connect Bangui by <a href="/wiki/Rail_transport" title="Rail transport">rail</a> to the <a href="/wiki/Transcameroon_Railway" title="Transcameroon Railway" class="mw-redirect">Transcameroon Railway</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Energy">Energy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Energy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Energy_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Energy in the Central African Republic">Energy in the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>The Central African Republic primarily uses <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity">hydroelectricity</a> as there are few other resources for energy.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Communications">Communications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Communications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote boilerplate seealso">See also: <a href="/wiki/Communications_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Communications in the Central African Republic" class="mw-redirect">Communications in the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>Presently, the Central African Republic has active television services, radio stations, <a href="/wiki/Internet_service_providers" title="Internet service providers" class="mw-redirect">internet service providers</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mobile_network_operator" title="Mobile network operator">mobile phone carriers</a>; <a href="/wiki/Socatel" title="Socatel">Socatel</a> is the leading provider for both internet and mobile phone access throughout the country. The primary governmental regulating bodies of telecommunications are the Ministère des Postes and Télécommunications et des Nouvelles Technologies. In addition, the Central African Republic receives international support on telecommunication related operations from <a href="/wiki/ITU-D" title="ITU-D">ITU Telecommunication Development Sector (ITU-D)</a> within the <a href="/wiki/International_Telecommunication_Union" title="International Telecommunication Union">International Telecommunication Union</a> to improve infrastructure.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CAR_classroom.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/CAR_classroom.jpg/220px-CAR_classroom.jpg" width="220" height="330" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/CAR_classroom.jpg/330px-CAR_classroom.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/00/CAR_classroom.jpg/440px-CAR_classroom.jpg 2x" data-file-width="533" data-file-height="800" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CAR_classroom.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Classroom in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Sam_Ouandja&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Sam Ouandja (page does not exist)">Sam Ouandja</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Education_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Education in the Central African Republic">Education in the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>Public education in the Central African Republic is free and is compulsory from ages 6 to 14.<sup id="cite_ref-ilab_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ilab-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup> However, approximately half of the adult population of the country is <a href="/wiki/Literacy" title="Literacy">illiterate</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Higher_education">Higher education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Higher education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Bangui" title="University of Bangui">University of Bangui</a>, a public university located in Bangui, includes a <a href="/wiki/Medical_school" title="Medical school">medical school</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Euclid_University" title="Euclid University" class="mw-redirect">Euclid University</a>, an international university in Bangui, are the two institutions of higher education in the Central African Republic.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Healthcare">Healthcare</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Healthcare">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Health_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Health in the Central African Republic">Health in the Central African Republic</a></div>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Caf_babies.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caf_babies.jpg/220px-Caf_babies.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caf_babies.jpg/330px-Caf_babies.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9f/Caf_babies.jpg/440px-Caf_babies.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3000" data-file-height="2000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Caf_babies.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Mothers and babies aged between 0 and 5 years are lining up in a Health Post at Begoua, a district of <a href="/wiki/Bangui" title="Bangui">Bangui</a>, waiting for the two drops of the oral <a href="/wiki/Polio_vaccine" title="Polio vaccine">polio vaccine</a>.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The largest hospitals in the country are located in the Bangui district. As a member of the <a href="/wiki/World_Health_Organization" title="World Health Organization">World Health Organization</a>, the Central African Republic receives vaccination assistance, such as a 2014 intervention for the prevention of a measles epidemic.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, female <a href="/wiki/Life_expectancy_at_birth" title="Life expectancy at birth" class="mw-redirect">life expectancy at birth</a> was 48.2 years and male life expectancy at birth was 45.1 years.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Women%27s_health" title="Women's health">Women's health</a> is poor in the Central African Republic. As of 2010, the country had the 4th highest <a href="/wiki/Maternal_mortality" title="Maternal mortality" class="mw-redirect">maternal mortality</a> rate in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Total_fertility_rate" title="Total fertility rate">total fertility rate</a> in 2014 was estimated at 4.46 children born/woman.<sup id="cite_ref-CIA_7-6" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIA-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> Approximately 25% of women had undergone <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> Many births in the country are guided by traditional birth attendants, who often have little or no formal training.<sup id="cite_ref-80" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Malaria" title="Malaria">Malaria</a> is endemic in the Central African Republic, and one of the leading causes of death.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup> According to 2009 estimates, the HIV/AIDS <a href="/wiki/Prevalence" title="Prevalence">prevalence</a> rate is about 4.7% of the adult population (ages 15–49).<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> Government expenditure on health was US$20 (PPP) per person in 2006<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_77-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> and 10.9% of total government expenditure in 2006.<sup id="cite_ref-hdrstats.undp.org_77-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-hdrstats.undp.org-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup> There was only around 1 physician for every 20,000 persons in 2009.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Central_African_Republic&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_the_Central_African_Republic" title="Human rights in the Central African Republic">Human rights in the Central African Republic</a></div>
<p>The 2009 Human Rights Report by the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">United States Department of State</a> noted that human rights in CAR were poor and expressed concerns over numerous government abuses.<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Human_Rights_Report_84-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Human_Rights_Report-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/United_States_State_Department" title="United States State Department" class="mw-redirect">U.S. State Department</a> alleged that major human rights abuses such as <a href="/wiki/Extrajudicial_punishment" title="Extrajudicial punishment">extrajudicial executions</a> by security forces, <a href="/wiki/Torture" title="Torture">torture</a>, beatings and <a href="/wiki/Rape" title="Rape">rape</a> of suspects and prisoners occurred with impunity. It also alleged harsh and life-threatening conditions in <a href="/wiki/Prison" title="Prison">prisons</a> and detention centers, arbitrary <a href="/wiki/Arrest" title="Arrest">arrest</a>, prolonged <a href="/wiki/Remand_(detention)" title="Remand (detention)">pretrial detention</a> and denial of a <a href="/wiki/Right_to_a_fair_trial" title="Right to a fair trial">fair trial</a>, restrictions on freedom of movement, official <a href="/wiki/Corruption" title="Corruption">corruption</a>, and restrictions on <a href="/wiki/Labor_rights" title="Labor rights">workers' rights</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Human_Rights_Report_84-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Human_Rights_Report-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The State Department report also cites widespread <a href="/wiki/Riot" title="Riot">mob violence</a>, the prevalence of <a href="/wiki/Female_genital_mutilation" title="Female genital mutilation">female genital mutilation</a>, discrimination against women and <a href="/wiki/Pygmy_peoples" title="Pygmy peoples">Pygmies</a>, <a href="/wiki/Human_trafficking" title="Human trafficking">human trafficking</a>, <a href="/wiki/Unfree_labour" title="Unfree labour">forced labor</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Child_labor" title="Child labor" class="mw-redirect">child labor</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> Freedom of movement is limited in the northern part of the country "because of actions by state security forces, armed bandits, and other nonstate armed entities", and due to fighting between government and anti-government forces, many persons have been <a href="/wiki/Internally_displaced_person" title="Internally displaced person">internally displaced</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-state.gov_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-state.gov-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Violence against children and women in relation to accusations of <a href="/wiki/Witchcraft" title="Witchcraft">witchcraft</a> has also been cited as a serious problem in the country.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_87-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Witchcraft is a criminal offense under the penal code.<sup id="cite_ref-unicef.org_87-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-unicef.org-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Freedom_of_speech" title="Freedom of speech">Freedom of speech</a> is addressed in the country's constitution, but there have been incidents of government intimidation of the media.<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Human_Rights_Report_84-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Human_Rights_Report-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> A report by the <a href="/wiki/International_Research_%26_Exchanges_Board" title="International Research &amp; Exchanges Board">International Research &amp; Exchanges Board</a>'s media sustainability index noted that "the country minimally met objectives, with segments of the legal system and government opposed to a free media system".<sup id="cite_ref-2009_Human_Rights_Report_84-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-2009_Human_Rights_Report-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Approximately 68% of girls are married before they turn 18,<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup> and the United Nations' <a href="/wiki/Human_Development_Index" title="Human Development Index">Human Development Index</a> ranked the country 179 out of 187 countries surveyed.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Bureau_of_International_Labor_Affairs" title="Bureau of International Labor Affairs">Bureau of International Labor Affairs</a> has also mentioned it in its last edition of the <i><a href="/wiki/List_of_Goods_Produced_by_Child_Labor_or_Forced_Labor" title="List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor">List of Goods Produced by Child Labor or Forced Labor</a></i>.</p>
